</table>
<p><b>Melbourne Victory Football Club</b> is an Australian professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">soccer</a> club based in <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a>. It competes in the country's premier competition, the <a href="/wiki/A-League" title="A-League">A-League</a>, under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_American_professional_sports_league_organization#Systems_around_the_world" title="North American professional sports league organization">licence</a> from <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_Australia" title="Football Federation Australia">Football Federation Australia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A-League_Licence_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-A-League_Licence-1">[1]</a></sup> Victory entered the competition in the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_A-League" title="2005–06 A-League">inaugural season</a> as the only Victorian-based club in the newly revamped domestic Australian league. The club has won three A-League Championships, three A-League Premierships, one Pre-Season Challenge Cup and one FFA Cup, the only club to have won all four Australian soccer trophies. They have also competed in the <a href="/wiki/AFC_Champions_League" title="AFC Champions League">AFC Champions League</a> on five occasions.</p>
<p>The club plays matches at both multi-use venues, <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Rectangular_Stadium" title="Melbourne Rectangular Stadium">Melbourne Rectangular Stadium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Docklands_Stadium" title="Docklands Stadium">Docklands Stadium</a>, with seated capacities of 30,050 and 56,347 respectively. A <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Victory_FC_Youth" title="Melbourne Victory FC Youth">youth team</a> competes in the <a href="/wiki/National_Youth_League_(Australia)" title="National Youth League (Australia)">National Youth League</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Victory_FC_(W-League)" title="Melbourne Victory FC (W-League)">women's team</a> competes in the <a href="/wiki/W-League_(Australia)" title="W-League (Australia)">W-League</a>. The youth and women matches are played at various locations across Melbourne, including <a href="/wiki/Lakeside_Stadium" title="Lakeside Stadium">Lakeside Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingston_Heath_Soccer_Complex" title="Kingston Heath Soccer Complex">Kingston Heath Soccer Complex</a> as well as Melbourne Rectangular Stadium.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Colours_and_badge">Colours and badge</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Melbourne_Victory_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Colours and badge">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>Melbourne Victory's club colours are navy blue, silver and white, which encompass the traditional state sporting colours of Victoria. In the Victory's inaugural A-League season, only the club badge displayed a <a href="/wiki/Chevron_(insignia)" title="Chevron (insignia)">chevron</a>, known colloquially as the "Big V", a symbol traditionally used by the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Australian_rules_football_team" title="Victoria Australian rules football team">Victoria Australian rules football team</a>. From the 2006–07 season the away strip was changed to a grey jersey with a white chevron on the front. This was an immediate hit with the club's supporters, and from the 2007–08 season onwards Melbourne's home jersey also sported the white chevron on the front. A new kit was introduced for the 2008 AFC Champions League<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> due to AFC rules requiring kits to have player numbers on the front of the uniform as well as the back, which would not fit well with the 'V' on the Victory's regular kit. For the 2009–10 season, Melbourne changed their away jersey to be a reverse of their home jersey; a white shirt with a blue chevron.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VictoryIntralot_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-VictoryIntralot-12">[12]</a></sup> In 2010, Melbourne wore the <a href="/wiki/Transport_Accident_Commission" title="Transport Accident Commission">TAC</a> 'seatbelt' shirt against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perth_Glory" title="Perth Glory">Perth Glory</a> in a charity event to raise awareness for the necessary use of seat belts in cars. On 16 June 2011, the current kits were announced via the club's <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> channel,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> which features a change to a fluoro yellow away jersey. Adidas were announced as the club's official kit manufacturer for five years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shirtSponsor_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-shirtSponsor-14">[14]</a></sup> For their 2013–14 kits, Melbourne Victory received backlash from supporters following the releasing of the kits, as the away kits had a large resemblance to rivals <a href="/wiki/Sydney_FC" title="Sydney FC">Sydney FC</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-au.fourfourtwo.com_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-au.fourfourtwo.com-15">[15]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_songs">Club songs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Melbourne_Victory_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Club songs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Stand_by_Me_(song)" title="Stand by Me (song)">Stand by Me</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Ben_E._King" title="Ben E. King">Ben E. King</a> is played prior to kick-off, when the Victory walk onto the field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> "Victory the Brave", a rearrangement for the club of <a href="/wiki/Scotland_the_Brave" title="Scotland the Brave">Scotland the Brave</a> by <a href="/wiki/Jim_Keays" title="Jim Keays">Jim Keays</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Masters_Apprentices" title="The Masters Apprentices">The Masters Apprentices</a>, is played after a home win, as is "Horses" by <a href="/wiki/Daryl_Braithwaite" title="Daryl Braithwaite">Daryl Braithwaite</a> at <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Rectangular_Stadium" title="Melbourne Rectangular Stadium">AAMI Park</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium">Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Melbourne_Victory_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aleaguefinal3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1025" data-file-width="3223" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Aleaguefinal3.jpg/325px-Aleaguefinal3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Aleaguefinal3.jpg/488px-Aleaguefinal3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Aleaguefinal3.jpg/650px-Aleaguefinal3.jpg 2x" width="325"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aleaguefinal3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/2007_A-League_Grand_Final" title="2007 A-League Grand Final">2007 A-League Grand Final</a> at Docklands Stadium</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Park_Stadium" title="Olympic Park Stadium">Olympic Park Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Docklands_Stadium" title="Docklands Stadium">Docklands Stadium</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Rectangular_Stadium" title="Melbourne Rectangular Stadium">Melbourne Rectangular Stadium</a></div>
<p>Melbourne were originally based at the 50-year-old <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Park_Stadium" title="Olympic Park Stadium">Olympic Park Stadium</a>, where they played all home matches during the 2005–06 A-League season. This stadium had seated areas only on the wings, with standing-room sandy terraces on the north and south ends. The average crowd during the first year was 14,158.</p>
<p>On 2 September 2006, Melbourne Victory played Sydney FC at the 56,000 capacity Docklands Stadium. The match was a runaway success in terms of crowds, with 39,730 in attendance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VictorySydney2006_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-VictorySydney2006-17">[17]</a></sup> As a result, the club moved all but one of their home games to the ground.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VictoryDocklandsMove_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-VictoryDocklandsMove-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>This move to such a large stadium was viewed with scepticism by many,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (June 2011)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> but proved to be an outstanding success, with the Grand Final held there. The average attendance rose to 27,728 for the 2006–07 season, 10,000 above the next highest in the A-League.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2015_A-League_Grand_Final_AAMI_Park_panorama.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="3328" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/2015_A-League_Grand_Final_AAMI_Park_panorama.jpg/325px-2015_A-League_Grand_Final_AAMI_Park_panorama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/2015_A-League_Grand_Final_AAMI_Park_panorama.jpg/488px-2015_A-League_Grand_Final_AAMI_Park_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/2015_A-League_Grand_Final_AAMI_Park_panorama.jpg/650px-2015_A-League_Grand_Final_AAMI_Park_panorama.jpg 2x" width="325"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2015_A-League_Grand_Final_AAMI_Park_panorama.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/2015_A-League_Grand_Final" title="2015 A-League Grand Final">2015 A-League Grand Final</a> at Melbourne Rectangular Stadium</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Prior to the 2006–07 season the club had planned to move to a new $190 million stadium being built to the east of the current Olympic Park complex.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewStadium_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-NewStadium-19">[19]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AAMI_Park" title="AAMI Park">new stadium</a> was originally expected to sit approximately 20,000 spectators (expandable to 25,000) and was to be completed by 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewStadium_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-NewStadium-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>These plans were revised after the Victory refused to commit to playing at such a small capacity stadium. On 23 May 2007, the club announced it had signed as a founding co-tenant of the new stadium, which would now be built to accommodate a maximum of 30,050 spectators with further renovations to 50,000 possible. However, further expansion in the near-term is unlikely as it was discovered during <a href="/wiki/Australia_2022_FIFA_World_Cup_bid" title="Australia 2022 FIFA World Cup bid">Australia's World Cup Bid</a> process that to build such an expansion would be prohibitively expensive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Docklands Stadium continued to serve as the club's only home ground until the completion of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AAMI_Park" title="AAMI Park">AAMI Park</a>. The club split its home games between the new stadium and Etihad Stadium from the 2010–11 A-League campaign onwards; the games of less importance or potential drawing power at the new stadium and the 'blockbusters' and finals matches at Etihad Stadium.</p>
<p>On 15 February 2014, Melbourne Victory played their Asian Champions League qualifying game against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muangthong_United" title="Muangthong United">Muangthong United</a> at <a href="/wiki/Kardinia_Park_(stadium)" title="Kardinia Park (stadium)">Kardinia Park</a> in Geelong due to AAMI Park and Etihad Stadium being unavailable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Support">Support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Melbourne_Victory_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>Melbourne Victory has the largest supporter base in Australia and has consistently set record highs in membership and attendance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Victory20k_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Victory20k-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2011, the Horda group was suspected to have stolen a banner from Melbourne Heart's Yarraside active group.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In the following games, Horda banners were banned, which led to great protest from the Northern Terrace active members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> At the following games, there was an increase in police and security present at the active area. Fans that were perceived as being "too aggressive" were escorted from the terrace, and in some cases fined or banned from the terrace.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> This led to the fans' anger escalating as they protested against the police control. On 2 February 2011, the fans from the North Terrace organised a silent protest for the Melbourne Victory – Newcastle Jets match. They left the North Terrace empty, and had a banner saying "No fans no past no future – without us you are nothing",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> "NT United". The banner was later confiscated by the police.</p>
<p>In February 2011, <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Police" title="Victoria Police">Victoria Police</a> said they were reluctant to cover Melbourne Victory games because of behaviour by fans that they claimed was unacceptable. Problems included violence, anti-social behaviour and the lighting of <a href="/wiki/Flare" title="Flare">flares</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 3 January 2014 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_Federation_of_Australia" title="Football Federation of Australia">Football Federation of Australia</a> charged both Melbourne Victory and <a href="/wiki/Western_Sydney_Wanderers_FC" title="Western Sydney Wanderers FC">Western Sydney Wanderers</a> with bringing the game into disrepute following violent fan behaviour before and during their game on 28 December 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Melbourne_Victory_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Derby_(A-League)" title="Melbourne Derby (A-League)">Melbourne Derby (A-League)</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Big_Blue_(A-League)" title="The Big Blue (A-League)">The Big Blue (A-League)</a></div>
<p>Rivalry exists with <a href="/wiki/Sydney_FC" title="Sydney FC">Sydney FC</a>, <span class="sortkey" style="display:none;">Melbourne City !</span><span class="sorttext"><a href="/wiki/Melbourne_City_FC" title="Melbourne City FC">Melbourne City</a></span> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adelaide_United" title="Adelaide United">Adelaide United</a>, as well as a budding rivalry with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Sydney_Wanderers" title="Western Sydney Wanderers">Western Sydney Wanderers</a>.</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="sortkey" style="display:none;">Melbourne City !</span><span class="sorttext"><a href="/wiki/Melbourne_City_FC" title="Melbourne City FC">Melbourne City</a></span> – (<a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Derby_(A-League)" title="Melbourne Derby (A-League)">Melbourne Derby</a>) Melbourne Victory's local rival is Melbourne City, which entered the competition in the 2010-11 season (as Melbourne Heart, before the name change in 2014), becoming the 2nd club in Melbourne. The rivalry reached a whole new level when Victory skipper Kevin Muscat was red carded for an unacceptable tackle on Heart player Adrian Zahra.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MuscatTackle_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-MuscatTackle-29">[29]</a></sup> Currently 5 former Victory players have switched to Melbourne Heart (City), with Mate Dugandžić doing the first ever direct switch from Victory to City in 2011. And arguably Harry Kewell in 2013, after being released by victory at the end of the 2012 season. There is some debate to whether he made a direct switch from victory to city (heart at the time), as he was a free agent when he made the switch. Currently no players have gone the other way (City to Victory)</li>
<li><span class="sortkey" style="display:none;">Sydney FC !</span><span class="sorttext"><a href="/wiki/Sydney_FC" title="Sydney FC">Sydney FC</a></span> – Sydney is considered Melbourne's major interstate rival, due to Melbourne and Sydney being Australia's two largest cities (see <a href="/wiki/Australian_regional_rivalries#Sydney_-_Melbourne_rivalry" title="Australian regional rivalries">Melbourne-Sydney rivalry</a>). Matches between the two teams are regularly controversial and bitter encounters. Strong tensions are also emerging between the supporters from opposing teams, evident in the sell-out crowds. The rivalry between the two teams was escalated further after Sydney beat Melbourne in the final match of the 2009–10 season to win the A-League Premiership, and again beat Melbourne in the 2010 A-League Grand Final. However, in season 2014/15, Victory reversed these feats, by first pipping Sydney to the A-League Premiership, in the normal 'home and away' season and weeks later beat them in the 2015 A-League Grand Final.</li>
<li><span class="sortkey" style="display:none;">Adelaide United !</span><span class="sorttext"><a href="/wiki/Adelaide_United_FC" title="Adelaide United FC">Adelaide United</a></span> – (The Original Rivalry). Melbourne Victory also has a rivalry with Adelaide United. This rivalry stems from the other football codes, where the interstate rivalry is big between Victorians and <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">South Australians</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Australian_regional_rivalries#South_Australia_and_Victoria" title="Australian regional rivalries">South Australia-Victoria rivalry</a>). There has also been altercations between sets of opposing fans in Melbourne and Adelaide. The rivalry has built up from previous encounters, when an incident between the then Adelaide United manager, <a href="/wiki/John_Kosmina" title="John Kosmina">John Kosmina</a>, and Victory skipper Kevin Muscat took place during a sideline altercation during a match in the 2006–07 season,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> and when Victory striker Ney Fabiano allegedly spat in the direction of Adelaide defender <a href="/wiki/Robert_Cornthwaite_(footballer)" title="Robert Cornthwaite (footballer)">Robert Cornthwaite</a> during Round 4 in the 2008–09 season he was banned for 9 matches; however, this was reduced to 6 after a successful appeal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Victory and Adelaide contested both the 2006–07 and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A-League_Grand_Final_2009" title="A-League Grand Final 2009">2008–09</a> Grand Finals, with Melbourne winning both.</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth_squad">Youth squad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Melbourne_Victory_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Youth squad">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Victory_FC_Youth" title="Melbourne Victory FC Youth">Melbourne Victory FC Youth</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate">Corporate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Melbourne_Victory_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Corporate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anthony_Di_Pietro_-_Melbourne_Victory.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1428" data-file-width="1430" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Anthony_Di_Pietro_-_Melbourne_Victory.jpg/200px-Anthony_Di_Pietro_-_Melbourne_Victory.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Anthony_Di_Pietro_-_Melbourne_Victory.jpg/300px-Anthony_Di_Pietro_-_Melbourne_Victory.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Anthony_Di_Pietro_-_Melbourne_Victory.jpg/400px-Anthony_Di_Pietro_-_Melbourne_Victory.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anthony_Di_Pietro_-_Melbourne_Victory.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Club <a href="/wiki/Chairman" title="Chairman">chairman</a> <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Di_Pietro" title="Anthony Di Pietro">Anthony Di Pietro</a> took charge in the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_A-League" title="2011–12 A-League">2011–12</a> pre-season following inaugural chairman <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Lord" title="Geoff Lord">Geoff Lord</a>'s resignation.</div>
</div>
</div>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;margin-left:1em;float:right">
<tr>
<th>Period</th>
<th><a href="/wiki/Chairman" title="Chairman">Chairman</a></th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2005–2011</td>
<td rowspan="1"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia"><img alt="Australia" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="1280" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Lord" title="Geoff Lord">Geoff Lord</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>2011–</td>
<td rowspan="1"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia"><img alt="Australia" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="1280" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Di_Pietro" title="Anthony Di Pietro">Anthony Di Pietro</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>As of 2015, the largest of around fifty shareholders of Melbourne Victory Ltd, an unlisted public company, is Mario Biasin, owner of construction company <a href="/wiki/Metricon" title="Metricon">Metricon</a>, followed by others including current Victory chairman <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Di_Pietro" title="Anthony Di Pietro">Anthony Di Pietro</a>, CEO of Premier Fruits Group.</p>
<p>Victory struggled to raise the initial $5 million equity capital to join the A-League in its first year and the FFA helped the club over the line by contributing franchise and set-up fees of about $500,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GeoffLordTakeover_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-GeoffLordTakeover-33">[33]</a></sup> The FFA took a ten per cent holding in the club in return, as well as having a representative on the Victory board.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GeoffLordTakeover_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-GeoffLordTakeover-33">[33]</a></sup> The shareholding was offered back to the club in 2007 and Geoff Lord and his partners – including Ron Peck, Richard Wilson and John Harris – raised the money to buy the shares.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GeoffLordTakeover_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-GeoffLordTakeover-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, it was announced that major shareholder, real estate investor Harry Stamoulis and fellow shareholder Robert Belteky, Managing Director of car parking company Care Park, along with some other minority shareholders, would offer their combined 35% stake in Melbourne Victory for sale to the general public, making part ownership of the club available to regular fans, a first for an A-League club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> However, despite payments already having been collected from fans by the facilitator of the sale <a href="/wiki/Deloitte" title="Deloitte">Deloitte</a>, on the 12 of November it was announced that the entire allocation of shares were eventually purchased "by a small number of long-term substantial shareholders".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Victory's commercial success has even surpassed many much longer established Melbourne <a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_League" title="Australian Football League">AFL</a> teams (with <a href="/wiki/Hawthorn_Football_Club" title="Hawthorn Football Club">Hawthorn</a> the only team to report a higher profit in 2014-15). Despite this, Melbourne Victory FC is not a "for profit" business, and as such the shareholders have never taken a dividend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsors">Sponsors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Melbourne_Victory_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Sponsors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On 5 December 2005, South Korean electronics giant Samsung became the club's major sponsor in a two-year deal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VictorySamsung_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-VictorySamsung-37">[37]</a></sup> This would ensure that Samsung would have their logo feature on the front and the back of Victory's home and away kits. Prior to the 2006–07 season, <a href="/wiki/KFC" title="KFC">KFC</a> were announced as Victory's sleeve sponsor, with their logo appearing on the sleeve of Victory's home and away kits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> On 28 January 2009, Samsung announced that they would not be renewing their sponsorship for the 2009–10 A-League season. Intralot became the Melbourne Victory's new major sponsor when they signed a two-season $2 million contract on 4 May 2009. Their logo subsequently featured on the front of Melbourne Victory's playing strip, starting from the 2009–10 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> On 6 August 2010, it was announced that law firm Florin Burhala Lawyers would be Melbourne Victory's official shorts sponsor for the 2010–11 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> On 1 June 2011, it was announced that human resources company Adecco Group signed a three-year deal as the club's major sponsor, replacing Intralot. As part of the deal, Adecco's logo will appear on the front of the club's playing strip.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Melbourne Victory announced on 16 June 2011 that they had signed a five-year deal with global sportswear giant Adidas as the club's official kit manufacturer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shirtSponsor_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-shirtSponsor-14">[14]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Records">Records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Melbourne_Victory_FC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Melbourne_Victory_FC_records_and_statistics" title="List of Melbourne Victory FC records and statistics">List of Melbourne Victory FC records and statistics</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Archie_Thompson-2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="913" height="289" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Archie_Thompson-2012.jpg/220px-Archie_Thompson-2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Archie_Thompson-2012.jpg/330px-Archie_Thompson-2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Archie_Thompson-2012.jpg/440px-Archie_Thompson-2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Archie_Thompson-2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Archie_Thompson" title="Archie Thompson">Archie Thompson</a> was Melbourne's first signing. He leads in most appearances &amp; most goals scored for the club.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Archie_Thompson" title="Archie Thompson">Archie Thompson</a> holds the team record for number of total games played with 224 matches. Thompson also holds the record for all-time highest goalscorer in all competitions with 95 goals.</p>
<p>Melbourne Victory's record win came against <a href="/wiki/Adelaide_United_FC" title="Adelaide United FC">Adelaide United</a> 6–0, on 18 February 2007, in the <a href="/wiki/2007_A-League_Grand_Final" title="2007 A-League Grand Final">2007 A-League Grand Final</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2007GrandFinal_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-2007GrandFinal-46">[46]</a></sup> Victory's record defeat was against rival <a href="/wiki/Sydney_FC" title="Sydney FC">Sydney FC</a>, in a 0–5 on 26 January 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VictoryvsSydney2014_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-VictoryvsSydney2014-47">[47]</a></sup> Melbourne Victory's record <a href="/wiki/FFA_Cup" title="FFA Cup">FFA Cup</a> win came against <a href="/wiki/Balmain_Tigers_FC" title="Balmain Tigers FC">Balmain Tigers FC</a> on the 4th of August 2015 with the score of 0–6.</p>
<p>The clubs highest home attendance is 50,333 for a league <a href="/wiki/The_Big_Blue_(A-League)" title="The Big Blue (A-League)">Big Blue</a> match on 8 December 2006, at <a href="/wiki/Docklands_Stadium" title="Docklands Stadium">Docklands Stadium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> The clubs highest home attendance for any match is 95,446 for pre-season <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exhibition_match" title="Exhibition match">friendly</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Cricket_Ground" title="Melbourne Cricket Ground">Melbourne Cricket Ground</a> on 24 July 2013, against <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
